13/01/2023, 08:30 - Shuvam CSE B: //Inter thread communication
class BankThread
{
	int balance = 10000;
	synchronized void withdraw(int amount)
	{
		System.out.println("Welcome to withdraw");
		System.out.println("Before withdraw balance is "+balance);
		if(amount>balance)
		{
			System.out.println("Insufficient balance...Please wait");
			try
			{
				wait();
			}
			catch(Exception obj5)
			{
				System.out.println("Exception occured");
			}
			System.out.println("Now required amount is available");
			balance = balance-amount;
			System.out.println("After withdraw balance is "+balance);
		}
		else
		{
			System.out.println("Now required amount is available");
			balance = balance-amount;
			System.out.println("After withdraw balance is "+balance);
		}
	}
	synchronized void deposit(int amount)
	{
		System.out.println("Welcome to depsoit");
		System.out.println("Before deposit balance is "+balance);
		balance = balance+amount;
		System.out.println("After deposit balance is "+balance);
		try
		{
			notify();
		}
		catch(Exception obj5)
		{
			System.out.println("Exception occured");
		}
	}
}
class Parent extends Thread
{
	BankThread ob;
	Parent(BankThread ob)
	{
		this.ob = ob;
	}
	public void run()
	{
		ob.deposit(35000);
	}
}
class Child extends Thread
{
	BankThread ob;
	Child(BankThread ob)
	{
		this.ob = ob;
	}
	public void run()
	{
		ob.withdraw(25000);
	}
}
class InterThreadCommunication
{
	public static void main(String args[])
	{
		BankThread ob = new BankThread();
		Parent obj1 = new Parent(ob);
		Child obj2 = new Child(ob);
		obj2.start();
		obj1.start();
	}
}

Greetings from All India Council for Technical Education

Yuva Sangam is an initiative of Government of India which focuses on conducting exposure tours of the youths comprising mainly students studying in Higher Educational institutions (HEIs) & some off-campus youths from one state to other states & vice versa. It provides an immersive experience of various facets of life, development landmarks, recent achievements and a youth connect in the host state. During their visits, the youths will have a multi¬≠ dimensional exposure under five broad areas ‚Äî Paryatan (Tourism), Parampara (Traditions), Pragati (Development), Paraspar Sampark (People-to-people connect), and Prodyogiki (Technology).

This is to inform that a civic programme is scheduled under EBSB: Yuva Sangam at 4:00 PM on 20.05.2023 at Shiksha 'O' Anusandhan University, Bhubaneswar, Odisha.

23/05/2023, 21:17 - Manohar CSE SIT: *Summer Internship Notice*
Subject: Full Stack Development Using Django
Why you will enroll for this course?
1.	You will never get a chance to study this course during your Engineering as it is not present in your course curriculum. 
2.	This course is the combination of Python, HTML, CSS, Java script, Bootstrap and Django. You will get all basic idea in programing to handle questions during placement drive.
3.	To build your career in IT industry you need to be a full stack developer i.e. you should be good in frontend and backend design.
4.	During placement drive you will get extra mileage among other students as the current need is this.
5.	The machine learning enthusiastic students will learn how to move their model into production environment. Email communication and user authentication can be learnt using Django. 
6.	Companies like Instagram, YouTube, Spotify, Dropbox, and many more are using Django as a backend.
7.	According to StackOverflow, 15% of the developers are using Django worldwide. 
8.	You can build your confidence in programming as it will be completely hands-on and interactive. No theory will be taught without practical implementation. 
9.	You will be guided for implementing of 2 projects i.e. 1 through classroom teaching and 1 by yourself during the class. This is enough to face the interviewer during placement drive. 
10.	In India, the average salary of a Django developer is 7 LPA.
This course will build your basics with live projects from scratch to overcome the gap of programming knowledge to fulfill your ultimate goal i.e. getting a job in good company. We will consider everyone as beginner to programming and teach accordingly so that you will gain a lot of thing from this course. 
 Date - 30/6/2023 to 22/7/2023
Time - 9.30am to 12.30pm

With Regards
Dr. Samaleswari Prasad Nayak
Course coordinator 
Department of CSE

24/05/2023, 20:06 - Manohar CSE SIT: *Hello Siliconites*

Silicon Students' Council is thrilled to present a groundbreaking initiative aimed at revolutionizing the learning experience for students facing challenges in various subjects. In an effort to foster a supportive academic environment, we are introducing evening remedial classes conducted by highly proficient senior students. This innovative approach not only addresses the academic needs of struggling students but also provides an exceptional opportunity for senior students to share their expertise and earn while doing so. Students who are interested to teach for these remedial classes can earn *200 rupees per hour*.

This new method of learning offers a win-win situation for both junior and senior students.  This mentorship-driven approach will empower struggling students to overcome their difficulties, build confidence, and achieve academic success.

students interested for mentoring need to fill this form by tomorrow 6:00p.m

11/06/2023, 23:01 - Manohar CSE SIT: Income effect: when price of a commodity falls money income remaining constant real income
increases. The consumer can buy more quantity of the commodity with his given income. If the
consumer chooses to buy the same amount of the commodity as before some money will be left
with him because he has to spend less on the commodity due to its lower price. This increase in
real income induces the consumer to buy more of that commodity. This is called income effect.
Substitution effect : Another important reason why the consumer consumes more when price fall
in substitution effect. When price of a commodity falls, it becomes relatively cheaper than its
substitutes . This indicates the consumer to substitute the commodity when price has fallen for
other commodities which have now becomes relatively dearer. For instance, tea and coffee are the
substitute goods. If the price of tea goes down, the consumer may substitute tea for coffee,
6
although price of coffee remain same. Therefore, with fall in price the demand will increase due
to unfavorable substitution effect.

15/06/2023, 19:54 - Manohar CSE SIT: Define Travelling Salesman Problem.
ans:It is an NP-complete problem that seeks to find the shortest possible route or tour that visits a given set of cities (or nodes) exactly once and returns to the starting city.Given a complete graph with a set of cities and the distances or costs between each pair of cities, the objective is to determine a tour that minimizes the total distance or cost.the goal is to find the optimal Hamiltonian cycle, which is a closed path that visits every city exactly once and has the minimum possible total distance.

15/06/2023, 19:54 - Manohar CSE SIT: Can we apply Bellman-Ford algorithm to find out the shortest path in a graph having
negative weight cycle?
ans:No, the Bellman-Ford algorithm cannot be directly applied to find the shortest path in a graph that contains a negative weight cycle. The Bellman-Ford algorithm is designed to handle graphs with negative edge weights, but it assumes that there are no negative weight cycles.

20/06/2023, 23:00 - Manohar CSE SIT: What is an Operating system? Give examples of some commonly used operating systems
An operating system (OS) is a software that manages computer hardware and provides a foundation for running applications. It acts as an intermediary between users and the computer hardware, enabling them to interact with the system and utilize its resources effectively. The OS performs essential functions such as managing memory, handling input and output devices, scheduling tasks, and providing a user interface.Example :Apple macOS, Microsoft Windows, Google's Android OS, Linux Operating System, and Apple iOS
20/06/2023, 23:00 - Manohar CSE SIT: What is the key difference between Application Software and System Software?

20/06/2023, 23:00 - Manohar CSE SIT: what is ipc?
interprocess communication (IPC) refers specifically to the mechanisms an operating system provides to allow the processes to manage shared data.
20/06/2023, 23:00 - Manohar CSE SIT: What is the necessity of context switching?
Context switching allows for multiprogramming, which means running multiple programs or processes concurrently on a single CPU. By rapidly switching between processes, the CPU can give the appearance of executing multiple tasks simultaneously, even though it executes each task in a time-sliced manner. This improves overall system throughput and resource utilization.

ans : Aging.Aging is a technique of gradually increasing the priority of processes that wait in the system for a long time.

20/06/2023, 23:00 - Manohar CSE SIT: Differentiate between CPU Bound and I/O Bound Processes.
A system is said to be I/O bound if the time taken to complete a computation is dependent on the period spent waiting for input/output operations to be completed. This is the complete opposite of a system being CPU bound where the tasks are determined solely on the performance of the CPU.
20/06/2023, 23:00 - Manohar CSE SIT: What is the major drawback of priority scheduling and suggest a solution for it?
The major drawback of priority scheduling is the possibility of starvation.The solution is aging.Aging is a technique that gradually increases the priority of a process over time if it has been waiting for an extended period. By increasing the priority of lower priority processes that have been waiting for a long time, the scheduler can ensure that they eventually get a chance to execute, even if higher priority processes frequently arrive.
20/06/2023, 23:00 - Manohar CSE SIT: Why do deadlocks occur? How are they detected by the operating system and resolved?

Deadlocks occur in a system when two or more processes are unable to proceed because each is waiting for a resource held by another process in the set. This situation creates a circular dependency where none of the processes can proceed, leading to a deadlock state. Deadlocks typically occur due to the following four necessary conditions:Mutual Exclusion,No Preemption,Hold and Wait,Circular Wait.
Techniques to detect and resolve deadlocks:
Deadlock Detection,Deadlock avoidance
20/06/2023, 23:00 - Manohar CSE SIT: Explain the role of base and limit register.
Base Register: The base register holds the starting physical address of the memory block allocated to a particular process. It specifies the base address or the beginning point of the memory region assigned to the process. When a process references memory locations, the base register is used to translate logical addresses to physical addresses by adding the base address to the logical address.

Limit Register: The limit register specifies the size or the length of the memory block allocated to a process. It indicates the maximum logical address that a process can reference within its allocated memory region. The limit register defines the range or the extent of memory accessible to the process.
20/06/2023, 23:00 - Manohar CSE SIT: Differentiate between LFU and MFU page replacement algorithms. 
LFU (Least Frequently Used):

The LFU algorithm selects the page with the least number of references or usage frequency for replacement.
MFU (Most Frequently Used):

The MFU algorithm selects the page with the highest number of references or usage frequency for replacement.
20/06/2023, 23:00 - Manohar CSE SIT: What are the essential goals of disk scheduling?
Improve Disk Performance,Reduce Response Time,Avoid Starvation,Minimize Head Movements

22/09/2023, 10:19 - Shuvam CSE B: Dear Students,
We wish to draw your attention to the growing prevalence of cybercrime cases not only in India but also in our own state of Odisha. Against this backdrop and with October designated as "Cyber Security Awareness Month," Odisha Police is taking proactive measures to combat this issue. We are pleased to announce the upcoming "Cyber Safety Campaign" scheduled to run from September 30th, 2023, to October 15th, 2023.
The primary aim of this campaign is to enhance awareness about cybercrime across different segments of society and age groups. We intend to educate elderly citizens, women, students, and youth on how to stay safe in the digital realm.
To make this initiative a resounding success, Odisha Police is seeking participation from all sections of society to help spread awareness about cybercrimes. It is believed that students from leading Engineering and Technical Institutions are particularly well-suited for this task due to their digital proficiency, influence within their peer groups, extensive online presence, effective communication skills, and the ability to amplify messages through social media.
In light of the above, Odisha Police introduce the "Cyber Volunteer" Program on September 30th, 2023, as an integral part of the "Cyber Safety Campaign." This program represents a collaboration between the police force and the academic community.
The students are requested to be a  Cyber volunteer to partner with Odisha Police in the "Cyber Safety Campaign" to support this important social cause. The processes to register as "Cyber Volunteers", additional information about the "Cyber Volunteer" program and the "Cyber Safety Campaign" can be found in the attached document.
We strongly encourage you to consider becoming a Cyber Volunteer and join us in the collective efforts against various forms of cybercrimes.
Sincerely,
Ramaprasad Panda
Dean, Administration & Student Affairs
Silicon Tech

17/11/2023, 11:20 - Sidharth Silicon: def calculate_likelihood_gaussian(df,feat_name,feat_val,Y,label):
    feat=list(df.columns)
    df=df[df[Y]==label]
    mean,std=df[feat_name].mean(),df[feat_name].std()
    p_x_given_y=(1/(np.sqrt(2*np.pi)*std)) * np.exp(-((feat_val-mean) **2/(2*std **2)))
    return p_x_given_y
17/11/2023, 11:20 - Sidharth Silicon: def naive_bayes_gaussian(df, X, Y):
    features = list(df.columns)[:-1]
    prior = calculate_prior(df, Y)
    Y_pred = []
    for x in X:
        labels = sorted(list(df[Y].unique()))
        likelihood = [1]*len(labels)
        for j in range(len(labels)):
            for i in range(len(features)):
                likelihood[j] *= calculate_likelihood_gaussian(df, features[i], x[i], Y, labels[j])
        post_prob = [1]*len(labels)
        for j in range(len(labels)):
            post_prob[j] = likelihood[j] * prior[j]
        Y_pred.append(np.argmax(post_prob))
    return np.array(Y_pred)

07/12/2023, 14:01 - Aditya Pandey Silicon: Attention: Unauthorized Mobile Phone Usage in Classrooms and Laboratories
Dear Students,
Subject: Strict Adherence to Mobile Phone Usage Policies
It has come to our attention that some students are engaging in unauthorized use of mobile phones during both theory and laboratory classes, a violation of the prescribed code of conduct outlined in the student handbook (refer to Chapter 27 at https://silicon.ac.in/wp-content/uploads/2021/07/Silicon-Student-Handbook-2020.pdf) .
We would like to remind all students that such behavior is strictly prohibited. Any unauthorized use of mobile phones in classrooms, including both laboratory and theory sessions, will result in the seizure of the mobile phone by the respective faculty members. The confiscated phones will be handed over to the respective Heads of Departments (H.O.D.s).
In such cases, the return of the mobile phone to the student is contingent upon the submission of an undertaking to the HOD, pledging to refrain from unauthorized use of cell phones in the future. Additionally, a fine of Rs. 500/- must be paid at the accounts section by the defaulting student. The collected phone can be reclaimed at the information desk in the director's office. We appreciate your cooperation in maintaining a conducive learning environment.
Sincerely,
Dr. Ramaprasad Panda
Dean, Administration & Student Affairs

27/12/2023, 10:15 - Shuvam CSE B: Que-5:-

Node impurity measures are used in decision tree algorithms to evaluate the homogeneity of a node. Some common impurity measures include:

1. *Gini Impurity:* It measures the probability of incorrectly classifying a randomly chosen element if it was randomly labeled according to the distribution of labels in the node.

2. *Entropy:* It calculates the level of disorder or randomness in a set. In decision trees, it measures the information gain when a node is split.

3. *Misclassification Error:* This measures the fraction of instances in a node that are misclassified. It is a simpler measure but less commonly used compared to Gini impurity and entropy.

The choice of impurity measure depends on the specific requirements of the problem, and different measures may lead to slightly different tree structures.
